## about.gitlab.com[](https://handbook.gitlab.com/handbook/engineering/projects/#about-gitlab-com)

## Buyer Experience[](https://handbook.gitlab.com/handbook/engineering/projects/#buyer-experience)

## discussion-automation[](https://handbook.gitlab.com/handbook/engineering/projects/#discoto)
Discoto (A mix of “DISCussion” and “AUTOmation”) is a discussion-automation tool. It automatically creates and propagates discussion summaries and helps keep discussions organized.

## Git[](https://handbook.gitlab.com/handbook/engineering/projects/#git)
Git is a free and open source distributed version control system designed to handle everything from small to very large projects with speed and efficiency.

## Gitalisk[](https://handbook.gitlab.com/handbook/engineering/projects/#gitalisk)
A high-performance Node.js native addon for querying Git repository status and metadata, powered by Rust and libgit2

## GitHost.io[](https://handbook.gitlab.com/handbook/engineering/projects/#githost)
Hosted version of GitLab
### Assignments[](https://handbook.gitlab.com/handbook/engineering/projects/#assignments-49)
## GitLab[](https://handbook.gitlab.com/handbook/engineering/projects/#gitlab)
This is the canonical development repository for GitLab. Open source code from this repository gets mirrored to GitLab-FOSS project.
This project is the source of the gitlab-ee distributions like omnibus-gitlab packages, docker images, AWS AMIs etc.
GitLab EE requires a license key to be used, without which only the CE functionality will be available.
### Assignments[](https://handbook.gitlab.com/handbook/engineering/projects/#assignments-50)

## gitlab-cli[](https://handbook.gitlab.com/handbook/engineering/projects/#gitlab-cli)
GLab is an open source GitLab CLI tool bringing GitLab to your terminal next to where you are already working with git and your code without switching between windows and browser tabs. Work with issues, merge requests, watch running pipelines directly from your CLI among other features.
### Assignments[](https://handbook.gitlab.com/handbook/engineering/projects/#assignments-58)

## GitLab.com COGS[](https://handbook.gitlab.com/handbook/engineering/projects/#gitlab-cog)
This is a group which contains a separate project for each COG used by the GitLab.com infrastructure.
A COG is an integration between the role of a node (or cluster) and a Chat application such as Slack. The COG allows the infrastructure node (or cluster) to post status and alerts into Chat Channels and also allows for commands to be issued in the Chat Channel that control the behavior of the infrastructure node/cluster.
### Assignments[](https://handbook.gitlab.com/handbook/engineering/projects/#assignments-61)
## GitLab.com - infrastructure Terraform files[](https://handbook.gitlab.com/handbook/engineering/projects/#gitlab-com-infrastructure)
Terraform - configuration and provisioning files for virtual machine nodes on production and staging
### Assignments[](https://handbook.gitlab.com/handbook/engineering/projects/#assignments-62)
## Gitlab.com - runbooks[](https://handbook.gitlab.com/handbook/engineering/projects/#gitlab-com-runbooks)
Describes system components, triage procedures, alert configuration, Grafana dashboards, metrics catalog, Prometheus recording rules for GitLab.com used by the Infrastructure department.
### Assignments[](https://handbook.gitlab.com/handbook/engineering/projects/#assignments-63)
Maintainers |  [![Andrew Newdigate](https://about.gitlab.com/images/team/picture_andrew-crop.jpg)Andrew Newdigate](https://handbook.gitlab.com/handbook/company/team/#andrewn)   
[Prometheus](https://www.prometheus.io/)[Redis](https://redis.io/)[Elasticsearch](https://www.elastic.co/elasticsearch/) [![Bob Van Landuyt](https://about.gitlab.com/images/team/bob-crop.jpg)Bob Van Landuyt](https://handbook.gitlab.com/handbook/company/team/#reprazent)   
[Ruby on Rails](https://rubyonrails.org/)[LFS](https://docs.gitlab.com/ee/topics/git/lfs/)[GraphQL](https://docs.gitlab.com/development/api_graphql_styleguide/)[Prometheus](https://www.prometheus.io/) [![Igor Wiedler](https://about.gitlab.com/images/team/igorwiedler-crop.jpg)Igor Wiedler](https://handbook.gitlab.com/handbook/company/team/#igorwwwwwwwwwwwwwwwwwwww)

## GitLab Design[](https://handbook.gitlab.com/handbook/engineering/projects/#gitlab-design)
GitLab Design is used to jumpstart design work through the use of our design library. It is intended to enable frequent, stable, and consistent contributions while making GitLab’s design open and transparent. This project helps facilitate design handoffs and design–development communication.

## GitLab Development Kit[](https://handbook.gitlab.com/handbook/engineering/projects/#gitlab-development-kit)
GitLab Development Kit (GDK) provides a collection of scripts and other resources to install and manage a GitLab installation for development purposes. The source code of GitLab is spread over multiple repositories and it requires Ruby, Go, Postgres/MySQL, Redis and more to run.
GDK helps you install and configure all these different components, and start/stop them when you work on GitLab.
### Assignments[](https://handbook.gitlab.com/handbook/engineering/projects/#assignments-72)
Maintainers |  [![Doug Barrett](https://about.gitlab.com/images/team/d.barrett-crop.jpg)Doug Barrett](https://handbook.gitlab.com/handbook/company/team/#dbarrett)

## GitLab FOSS[](https://handbook.gitlab.com/handbook/engineering/projects/#gitlab-foss)
This is a mirror of GitLab codebase with all the proprietary code removed.
Development happens in the canonical repository at GitLab. This repository is updated periodically with changes from there.
This project is the source of the gitlab-ce distributions like omnibus-gitlab packages, docker images, AWS AMIs etc.

## GitLab MailRoom[](https://handbook.gitlab.com/handbook/engineering/projects/#gitlab-mail_room)
This fork of `mail_room` contains some merged functionality that GitLab requires, so this mirror fork is to help us release custom functionality. `mail_room` is a configuration based process that will listen for incoming e-mail and execute a delivery method when a new message is received.
### Assignments[](https://handbook.gitlab.com/handbook/engineering/projects/#assignments-87)

## GitLab Triage[](https://handbook.gitlab.com/handbook/engineering/projects/#gitlab-triage)
This gem aims to enable project managers and maintainers to automatically triage Issues and Merge Requests in GitLab projects based on defined policies.
### Assignments[](https://handbook.gitlab.com/handbook/engineering/projects/#assignments-108)

## gitlab-ui[](https://handbook.gitlab.com/handbook/engineering/projects/#gitlab-ui)
UI component library written in Vue.js. Use [](https://gitlab-org.gitlab.io/gitlab-ui/)<https://gitlab-org.gitlab.io/gitlab-ui/> to see all the components. Every frontend engineer at GitLab is a reviewer of this project. However, the reviewers below are part of the gitlab-ui working group, and it’s recommended to ping one of them in a non-trivial MR.
### Assignments[](https://handbook.gitlab.com/handbook/engineering/projects/#assignments-109)

## GitLab Workhorse[](https://handbook.gitlab.com/handbook/engineering/projects/#gitlab-workhorse)
Gitlab-workhorse is a smart reverse proxy for GitLab. It handles “large” HTTP requests such as file downloads, file uploads, Git push/pull and Git archive downloads.
### Assignments[](https://handbook.gitlab.com/handbook/engineering/projects/#assignments-115)

## Merge Train[](https://handbook.gitlab.com/handbook/engineering/projects/#merge-train)
Merge Train is a project used to automatically merge changes from a source repository into a target repository. Changes can be merged using git merge, or by copying over all changes except for proprietary files such as the ee/ directory in GitLab. In both cases merge conflicts are handled automatically.

## Release CLI[](https://handbook.gitlab.com/handbook/engineering/projects/#release-cli)
The GitLab Release CLI consumes instructions in the :release node of the .gitlab-ci.yml to create a Release object in GitLab Rails. GitLab Release is a CLI application written in Golang.

## Secret Detection Response Service[](https://handbook.gitlab.com/handbook/engineering/projects/#secret-detection-response-service)
A service to determine the status of tokens, classifying them as active, inactive, or unknown. This service helps identify potential security risks associated with active or unknown tokens in GitLab projects.
### Assignments[](https://handbook.gitlab.com/handbook/engineering/projects/#assignments-194)
## sectypes[](https://handbook.gitlab.com/handbook/engineering/projects/#sectypes)
A collection of schemas and parsers for various security related and security adjacent formats, clients and documents.

## version.gitlab.com[](https://handbook.gitlab.com/handbook/engineering/projects/#version.gitlab.com)
VersionDot application hosted by GitLab.
The app provides version upgrade information to self hosted instances and receives product usage data payloads called Service Ping. It is owned by the [Analytics Instrumentation Group](https://handbook.gitlab.com/handbook/engineering/development/analytics/analytics-instrumentation/).

## Finding a reviewer[](https://handbook.gitlab.com/handbook/engineering/projects/#finding-a-reviewer)
In addition to the lists on this page, the [GitLab review workload dashboard](https://gitlab-org.gitlab.io/gitlab-roulette/) provides an interface to find available reviewers and maintainers.
